The latest host table has Chaosnet host APIARY-10 at 13036, and
includes the latest NIC table.  I deleted SCRC-CUPID from our copy of
HSTNIC, since it collides with an entry in one of the other files.
Whoever maintains HSTSYM/HSTSYI should fix this.

LispM network hackers:  I also installed OZ:SRC:<S.SITE>HOSTS.TEXT, so
if someone recompiles the LispM Rel4 site files, etc., AP10 will be on
the air.  If MIT's Chaosnet namespace server (LM15) ever comes back
up, it can be made to gobble the tables from MC, so that AP10 would be
known in Rel5 systems.

Date: Friday, 23 December 1983, 11:26-EST
From: Kent M Pitman <KMP at MIT-MC>
Subject: Changes to OZ:SRC:<S.SITE>HOSTS.TEXT
To: INFO-HOSTS at MC
Cc: KMP at MC

I am not sure I followed accepted protocol here but could find
no documentation on how to do this, so please read carefully and
someone let me know if (and if so, why) the following changes
were inappropriate...

I edited OZ:SRC:<S.SITE>HOSTS.TEXT in the following ways:

 * System type for host BING-CROSBY was USER. I changed it to LISPM.

 * MC's list of nicknames was such that the DM nicknames came last.
   I think this was causing things to think MC's short name was MC.
   It appears (from experimentation, I didn't read the code) that the
   LAST shortest name which is last in the list of nicknames is what gets
   used. If this is true, should it be documented?

I did not edit MC:SYSENG;HOSTS > and MC:SYSENG;HSTMIT > because they
both already had these changes.

Is MC:SYSENG;HOSTS > supposed to be the same as OZ:SRC:<S.SITE>HOSTS.TEXT?
There is no documentation in either file suggesting the two need to be
kept compatible by installing one to the other when changes occur; is that
what is supposed to happen? If so, it should be documented in one or both
files. There is a comment at the top of OZ:SRC:<S.SITE>HOSTS.TEXT which 
mentions a file called HSTMIT which needs to be kept up to date, but that
comment does not mention that HSTMIT is not an OZ file at all, but an MC file.
At the very least, the comment in OZ:SRC:<S.SITE>HOSTS.TEXT should be fixed.

If indeed MC:SYSENG;HOSTS > and OZ:SRC:<S.SITE>HOSTS.TEXT are supposed to
be the same file, the OZ copy is out of date and/or out of synch and should
be brought up to date.
-kmp

Date: 8 December 1983 00:31 EST
From: David C. Plummer <DCP @ MIT-MC>
To: INFO-HOSTS @ MIT-MC, BUG-TWENEX @ MIT-MC, CSTACY @ MIT-MC,
    LispM-Networks @ SCRC-TENEX

From MC:SYSENG;HSTNIC > (the NIC host table)

HOST : 10.0.0.44 : MIT-XX,XX : DEC-2060T : TOPS20 : TCP/TELNET,TCP/FTP,TCP/SMTP,TCP/TIME,TCP/SUPDUP,TCP/MLDEV :

The last two items are complete bullshit.  MLDEV only exists
between ITSs, and Twenex has a hard enough time doing SUPDUP on
Chaos connections that I doubt it can do TCP/SUPDUP.  Besides, I
just tried it and got a refusal.  Therefore,

(1) Somebody should contact the NIC and have the two entries
    removed.
(2) Somebody (CStacy) should add this to the list of hand changes
    to make to the NIC file when new ones are slurped.
(3) Somebody at Symbolics should remove the two entries from XX's
    namespace object.

I am going to edit them out of version 322 and write it back as
322.

        The HOSTS3 program (which happenned to be running on MC) barfed on the
        HSTSYI file with some kind of syntax error, I forget the exact text of
        the message.  I just now tried it by itself, and it complained that
        network 18.0.0.0 was undefined and about some host address collisions
        within HSTSYI.  The current state is that HOSTS3 won't write a binary
        file from just HSTSYI.

    My understanding is that HSTSYI is supposed to be one of the
    INSERT files with HSTNIC.  I.e., it is a brother of HSTMIT.  It
    isn't supposed to be compiled separately, which is why it
    complains about network 18.0.0.0.  What happens when you
    uncomment it in HOSTS MASTER and try it?

No, the original problem occurred trying to compile the entire set in
the usual fashion.  The original error was not about the undefined
network, it was one of the syntax errors (missing colon or something
like that; I forget which one.)  However, I just now put HSTSYI back
in and it seems to work (gets only warning errors and produces the
binaries.)  If someone did not fix HSTSYI since I had the problem,
then the error must have been in another file and there is a bug in
HOSTS3's error reporting.

So, anyway, HSTSYI is back in HOSTS MASTER now.

HSTMIT 132 and HOSTS 678 on MC add MIT-FRANK-SINATRA, a 3600 on the 8th floor playroom
at Chaosnet address 13057.  I also created a namespace server object for the host.

While recompiling the site files on OZ, I manually edited HSTTBL.LISP to position
the MIT-DM nicknames for MC in the middle of MC's host name list, because I was
tired of seeing "DM:" instead of "MC:" in Release 4 software.

I removed the Symbolics Internet hosts from the HOSTS MASTER file on MC, since
it would not compile with that input; there is something screwed up about the
entries in the file. I suspect that unknown machine types were used in the entries.

I flusged MIT-AI-RESERVED from the HOSTS file.  Now, mind you that entry has been
there for a year and not caused any trouble, so whoever's parser cannot handle
it is broken.  However, this host is defined in the HSTNIC file, and needn't
be defined ho HSTMIT or HOSTS or anything anyway.

Until I get a demon to hack the NIC host table server, please keep the version
numbers on HSTNIC the same as the version which was FTPd from the NIC, even
if you make local modifications to it. (Be sure to install it properly though.
I know this is sort of a screw, but it will get fixed eventually.)

Compiled and installed new host table on MC and ML, and new 3600 site files on OZ.

Received: from PEACE by SCRC-QUABBIN with CHAOS; Thu 17-Nov-83 08:57:21-EST

Subject: making MC host tables
To: info-hosts@MIT-MC.ARPA
Message-ID: <831117085408.3.Hornig@QUABBIN.SCRC.Symbolics>

Whenever a new host table comes over from the NIC, you must do the
following surgery on it before you can compile it:

  Delete the name	ARTHUR	from PURDUE
			COYOTE	from SU-COYOTE
			FORD	from FORD1
			MERLIN	from PURDUE-MERLIN
			EDDIE	from UW-EDDIE

  Comment out the entries for MIT-BR-ETHERNET and MIT-GW-LCS.

     0:00:33 MONTR	 !@Update-Host-Tables
     0:00:50 USER	Checking foreign file SYSENG;HSTNIC > ... No change.
     0:01:12 USER	Checking foreign file SYSENG;HSTMIT > ... New version: 125

     0:02:06 USER	   Inserting file PS:<SYSTEM>HOSTS.NIC.323
     0:05:12 USER	   Inserting file PS:<SYSTEM>HOSTS.MIT.125

     0:05:13 USER	Error on line 41: Garbage where end of line expected
    ;WHO SAYS THESE EXTRA COMMAS ARE NECESSARY?  Please leave a pointer!
    ; I (Marty) am going to delete them, unless someone can explain what
    ; parser can't figure out to set all the fields left on a line to some
    ; default values.  Trying to compile this file gives errors.
    ;Extra commas necessary
    HOST MIT-AI-RESERVED,	2/6,USER,,,
The comment was there when I started, the commas were not.  Since the
parser that converts HSTMIT to the Symbolics Release 5 host database
needs them, and the comment was there, I added them.  As an alternetive,
I will comment out the line.

entries in HSTSU are all bogus.  I hear that the wrong addresses
have been compiled for SU-NET machines like LOTS which are not
defined elsewhere (ie., in HSTNIC).

    From: Dan Ottenheimer  <DANO at MIT-JCF>
    Date: 2-NOV-1983 09:08
    Subj:	Sending Mail to the JCF
    Months ago, the JCF intended to use a PDP-11 as a gateway to CHAOSnet.
    The host names MIT-JCF-VAX and MIT-JCF-11 were established with this in
    mind.
    This concept was (temporarily?) abandoned due to lack of software.  The
    two host names were thrown out in favor of MIT-JCF.  However, it seems
    as though it takes quite a while forhost name changes to make its way
    to all of the tables on the network...

MC is were the master host tables for MIT live, so changes made there will
propagate to everywhere necessary. INFO-HOSTS@MC are the people who deal
with changes in the lists, so i am forwarding your information there. if
you can get to MC you can change the host tables yourself; otherwise you
can supply the information to the list and ask someone else to change it.
if you are dealing with JCF's net connection you might want to be added to
INFO-HOSTS, although a lot of the notices that are sent on it wouldn't be
relevant to you.

Date: 23 Aug 1983 1924-EDT
From: J. Noel Chiappa <JNC@MIT-XX>
To: DPH@MIT-MC, INFO-HOSTS@MIT-MC
cc: JNC@MIT-XX
In-Reply-To: Your message of 17-Aug-83 1925-EDT

	Among our chief weapons are surprise, fear, obscure error messages
and a ruthless devotion to nit-picking detail.
	Yadda-yadda, warden, yadda-yadda.

	Well, after some toying with this, it appears that there are
several obscure problems (there aren't any typos), apparently caused
by conflicts with the info in HSTNIC, although the error messages are
so bizarre it's hard to tell. (E.g. moving MIT-XX-11 from LCS subnet
10 to 12 causes the message "Duplicate host name MIT-XX-11 = PDP-11,
PDP11" to appear; perhaps there's a rhyme to all this, but I must admit
it escapes me.)
	I guess there are several options; the most local is for me
to get HSTNIC done right (I sent some corrections off a while ago,
but they appear not to have made it in yet) and then update HSTMIT,
although the new version of HSTNIC might not compile correctly then
until I fix HSTMIT. Another option is to flush duplicate entries
(I'd probably leave most MIT server hosts in the NIC table only, since
they might want to be able to get mail from hither and thither, etc)
and only leave random machines in HSTMIT. Finally, perhaps a HOSTS3
wizard (I started to look at the source, and decided that it was
beyond my modest MIDAS talents) could look at the problem and either
tell me how to win, or perhaps (if HOSTS3 is deemed to be losing
somehow, e.g. by not allowing machines to have different sets of
addresses in different tables - note that almost none of my changes
had conflicting machine names at the same address) fixing HOSTS3.
Certainly, the error messages are slightly obscure.
	Then, of course, I could always punt.
		Noel

PS - anyone who can identify the second obscure quotation gets a
winner-gram.
-------

Date: 15 August 1983 02:52 EDT
From: Ken Harrenstien <KLH @ MIT-MC>

    zues-crew @ MIT-SPEECH

    Date: Friday, 12 August 1983, 16:48-EDT
    From: dph at MIT-XX

    HSTMIT 68 and HOSTS 626 fix brain damage by twits who screw around where
    they think they understand but they don't.  Lisp machines MERLIN,
    AVATAR, POLAR, KOALA and BOOBOO were grossly out of alphabetical order
    in both files (some of them weren't even in the same places in both

    no easy trick.

is not alphabetically sorted.  And while doing this, you might consider
parsing the RFC-810 format directly.  Otherwise you will forever have
to play catchup with changes in the rest of the world.  I am not saying
that you have to do this; just trying to point out one way to reduce
the grief and tedium involved.

Received: from SRI-NIC by SU-SCORE.ARPA with TCP; Sat 2 Jul 83 12:51:16-PDT
Date:  2 Jul 1983 1227-PDT
From: DYER at SRI-NIC (Mary Stahl Dyer)
Subject: New NIC host tables generated
To: Host-table-updates-list:
cc: dyer at SRI-NIC

An updated version of the DoD internet host table is available from
the Network Information Center via the NIC Host Name Server (RFC 811).
To access the server, open a TCP telnet connection to the Host Name
Server port (101 decimal) and enter a command line containing one of
the following keys:
 
   HNAME <name>     --search for name
   HADDR <addr>     --search for address
   ALL              --dump entire table
 
   (all of the above display entries in the standard format)
 
   ALL-INGWAY       --dump TENEX/TOPS-20 gateway file
   ALL-HSTNAM       --dump TENEX host name file
   ALL-MULTINET     --dump TENEX Internet host name file
   VERSION          --shows version number of current table
 
<name> is a name or nickname
<addr> is a dotted Internet address (RFC 796), for example 10.0.0.73,
       composed of the four octets of the full 32 bit Internet address,
       each expressed in decimal
 
The command line is terminated by carriage return.
 
If you still have access via FTP only, the files to obtain are:
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HOSTS.TXT, the new format host table
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HSTNAM.TXT, the TENEX/TOPS-20 style table
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HSTNAM.MULTINET, the TENEX/TOPS-20 style Internet table
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>INTERNET.GATEWAYS
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HOSTS2.BIN
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HOSTS3.BIN
 
 
   Mary Dyer
   Network Information Center
-------

Date: Sat 25 Jun 83 21:12:32-PDT
From: Mark Crispin <MRC@SU-SCORE.ARPA>
Subject: MIT hosts
To: INFO-HOSTS@MIT-MC.ARPA
Postal-Address: 725 Mariposa Ave. #103; Mountain View, CA 94041
Phone: (415) 497-1407 (Stanford); (415) 968-1052 (residence)

For the non-MIT world, in particular the TOPS-20 world, neither the MIT
nor the HOSTS3 host table is used.  Instead, we register the names of
various interesting hosts which we can deliver mail to by relaying through
the Internet MIT hosts.

We do this under the assumption that it's impossible to keep an accurate
table of what's at MIT up to date, and that we really aren't interested in
the Chaos addresses or of things like Lisp machines which non-MIT'ers
wouldn't address.

The official version of this registry is [SU-SCORE]MRC:<MM>DOMAINS.TXT;
TOPS-20 systems install it on their MAIL:DOMAINS.TXT.  (Note that Score's
MAIL:DOMAINS.TXT is different; it doesn't include the SUnet hosts since
Score is on SUnet and has the real registry available for it).

If some nice MIT person would like to try to keep the MIT information in
this registry up to date, I would gratefully appreciate it.

-- Mark --

PS: this registry deliberately doesn't include LCSnet hosts, since they are
presumably registered in the NIC table.
-------

Date:  7 June 1983 22:42 edt
From:  Saltzer at MIT-MULTICS
To:  David C. Plummer <DCP at MIT-MC>
cc:  PAO at MIT-MC, INFO-HOSTS at MIT-MC, 
     MIT-NETWORK-GROUP at MIT-MC
In-Reply-To:  Message of 7 June 1983 12:13 edt from David C. Plummer

One problem with tacking all the Tech Square Ethernets end to end is
that we are going to hit the 500-meter limit pretty soon.  The way
things are going, I can see a loop around each floor, since there are
getting to be quite a few IBM PC's that want to be on the Ethernet, and
for economy reasons they want to use their builtin transceiver--which
means that the Ethernet has to loop by each PC.

So I suppose we are going to end up with several Ethernets whether we
want them or not.

    ...
    This is losing.  Now there are THREE ethernets at Tech Square
    (ninth floor, fifth floor, and third floor).  At the very least,
    the ninth floor and the third floor should be connected.  When
    the fifth floor changes from experimental to service, it should
    be spliced in as well.  The current situation is just putting
    itsy-bitsy little Ethernets all over the place connected by the
    main chaos-hardware net, where it should be a coherent conversion
    to Ethernet.

Patience, patience.  The reason we haven't run a cable down here is that LCS
is going to run the 9th floor ethernet down to the second floor, and we'll
just be a subnet off that (it'll run conveniently through our phone closet).
They bought more cable than they need; they have 1000 feet.  If anyone wants
to buy some, contact Joe Ricchio.

We may eventually hack things so that the cable they've run is a separate
subnet, distinct from the ninth floor subnet, and the 9th floor, 3rd floor,
5th floor and 2nd floor nets are all subnets off it.  But first let's let
them get the cable run.

    I changed HSTMIT and HOSTS to add subnet 60 and put MIT-VULCAN and NE43-3A
    on it as hosts 30100 and 30120, respectively.  I did not generate new binaries,
    however.
This is losing.  Now there are THREE ethernets at Tech Square
(ninth floor, fifth floor, and third floor).  At the very least,
the ninth floor and the third floor should be connected.  When
the fifth floor changes from experimental to service, it should
be spliced in as well.  The current situation is just putting
itsy-bitsy little Ethernets all over the place connected by the
main chaos-hardware net, where it should be a coherent conversion
to Ethernet.

Date: 6 June 1983 12:12 EDT
From: Patrick G. Sobalvarro <PGS @ MIT-MC>
To: INFO-HOSTS @ MIT-MC
cc: GREN @ MIT-MC

We were unable to compile the new host tables with HOSTS3, because of
duplicate address errors on 4 LCS hosts: MIT-BRIDGE and MIT-BR-ETHERNET, and
MIT-GW and MIT-GW-LCS.  First case:
  10:44:16 USER	Duplicate address 18.2.0.7 = MIT-BR-ETHERNET, MIT-BRIDGE
  10:44:17 USER	Duplicate address 18.8.0.4 = MIT-GW-LCS, MIT-GW

The HSTNIC file had the entry

  HOST : 18.8.0.5, 18.10.0.5 : MIT-BRIDGE,MIT-BR,BRIDGE : PDP-11 : MOS : IP :

for MIT-BRIDGE and 

  HOST : 18.2.0.7 : MIT-BR-ETHERNET : PDP-11 : MOS : IP :

for MIT-BR-ETHERNET.  The HSTMIT file had the following entry:

  HOST MIT-BRIDGE,	[LCS 10/5,LCS 12/5,LCS 2/7,CHAOS 420],USER,MOS,PDP11,[MIT-BR,BRIDGE]

The error was caused by MIT-BRIDGE having one of MIT-BR-ETHERNET's addresses.
I changed HSTMIT to read:

  HOST MIT-BRIDGE,	[LCS 10/5,LCS 12/5,CHAOS 420],USER,MOS,PDP11,[MIT-BR,BRIDGE]

assuming LCSnet folks would be more likely to get the NIC table right than
the MIT table.

Second case:
  10:49:38 USER	Duplicate address 18.2.0.7 = MIT-BR-ETHERNET, MIT-BRIDGE
  10:49:38 USER	Duplicate address 18.8.0.4 = MIT-GW-LCS, MIT-GW

The HSTNIC file had the entries:

  GATEWAY : 10.0.0.77, 18.10.0.4 : MIT-GW,MIT-GATEWAY : PDP-11 : MOS : IP/GW,GW/DUMB :

  HOST : 18.8.0.4 : MIT-GW-LCS : PDP-11 : MOS : IP :

and the HSTMIT file had the entry

  HOST MIT-GW,		[0/77,LCS 10/4],USER,MOS,PDP11,[GW,MIT-GATEWAY]

Assuming this was a radix error (HSTMIT is octal, HSTNIC is decimal), I
changed HSTMIT to read

HOST MIT-GW,		[0/115,LCS 12/4],USER,MOS,PDP11,[GW,MIT-GATEWAY]

again making it agree with the NIC tables.

Note that I also changed GW's Arpa address to 115 in HSTMIT, because it also
looked like a radix error.

Received: from SRI-NIC by SU-SCORE.ARPA with TCP; Fri 3 Jun 83 18:12:51-PDT
Date:  3 Jun 1983 1747-PDT
From: HAL at SRI-NIC
Subject: New NIC host tables
To: host-table-updates: ;
cc: nic at SRI-NIC

An updated version of the DoD internet host table is available from
the Network Information Center via the NIC Host Name Server (RFC 811).
To access the server from a TCP host, open a TCP telnet connection to
the Host Name Server port (101 decimal) and enter a command line
containing one of the following keys:
 
   HNAME <name>     --search for name
   HADDR <addr>     --search for address
   ALL              --dump entire table
 
   (all of the above display entries in the standard format)
 
   ALL-INGWAY       --dump TENEX/TOPS-20 gateway file
   ALL-HSTNAM       --dump TENEX host name file
 
<name> is a name or nickname
<addr> is a dotted Internet address (RFC 796), for example 10.0.0.73,
       composed of the four octets of the full 32 bit Internet address,
       each expressed in decimal
 
The command line is terminated by carriage return.
 
NCP hosts may access the server by opening a connection to socket 101
decimal.  
 
If you still have access via FTP only, the files to obtain are:
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HOSTS.TXT, the new format host table
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HSTNAM.TXT, the TENEX/TOPS-20 style table
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HSTNAM.MULTINET
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>INTERNET.GATEWAYS
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HOSTS2.BIN
   [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>HOSTS3.BIN
 
 
   Mary Dyer
   Network Information Center
-------

Date: 22 March 1983 21:28 EST
From: Christopher C. Stacy <CSTACY @ MIT-MC>
Subject:  New ITS host table procedures.
To: INFO-HOSTS @ MIT-MC
cc: CSTACY @ MIT-MC


ITS now uses the HOSTS3 style host tables, making HOSTS2 obsolete.

ARPAnet hosts no longer need be updated manually by us.  Instead, the
NIC host table is automatically slurped in and munched.  The NIC table
now tends to be more up to date than HOSTS2 has been. All we need do
is FTP a copy here when it changes; I'll plan on taking care of that.
Any hosts which talk Internet should be mentioned in the NIC table.

Our MIT local-network hosts (ie., MIT Chaosnet, LCSnet, Symbolics
Ethernets) should be updated in the file SYSENG;HSTMIT >. The format
is similar to HOSTS2 and should be easy to follow.  No foreign people
should ever need to modify this table.  

Any Internet host entries in HSTMIT (for example for Chaosnet hosts
which are also Internet hosts, like MIT-MC) should agree with what is
in NIC table.  Our copy of the NIC table is kept in SYSENG;HSTNIC >.

Foreign local-nets (ie., SU/MIT/PARC/CMU ethernets) are updated in the
file SYSENG;HSTSU >.  At the end of HSTMIT and HSTSU files is a list
of the networks which the file is concerned with.

Someone can also continue to update HOSTS2 if they want, although
updates to that database will not be noticed by ITS.

The mailing list INFO-HOSTS on MC now points to two sublists:
INFO-HOSTS2 and INFO-HOSTS3.  INFO-HOSTS2 is the SU-SCORE mailing
list, and INFO-HOSTS3 is where other people should get on.  If you
want to get on INFO-HOSTS@MC, send mail to INFO-HOSTS-REQUEST@MIT-MC.

Updates should be sent to INFO-HOSTS@MIT-MC, so that everyone (even
the HOSTS2 users at Stanford and place) can see the notices, and
update their tables.  The file MC:DSK:SYSEN2;HSTINF RECENT has an
archiveof the mail send to INFO-HOSTS@MIT-MC.

Cheers,
Chris

Date:     8 Mar 83 6:50:44 EST (Tue)
From:     Mike Muuss <mike@Brl-Bmd.ARPA>

Subject:  BRL hosts to be updated in NIC Table

Date:     7 Mar 83 22:36:39 EST (Mon)
From:     Mike Muuss <mike@Brl-Bmd.ARPA>
To:       NIC@Sri-Nic.ARPA
cc:       Gurus@Brl-Bmd.ARPA, Info-Host@Mit-Mc.ARPA
Subject:  BRL hosts to be updated in NIC Table

I have another batch of updates to the NIC tables, as we finally converge
on a reasonably stable network numbering configuration here at BRL.

First, an important piece of news:  our gateway is now operating correctly,
and will be going production really soon.

To aid in editing the host tables, I'll try to be very explicit:

--- #1

Was:
HOST : 10.3.0.29 : BRL-BMD,BMD70 : PDP-11/70 : UNIX : TCP/TELNET,TCP/FTP,TCP/SMTP,TCP/TIME :

Should be changed to:
HOST : 192.5.21.1 : BRL-BMD,BMD70 : PDP-11/70 : UNIX : TCP/TELNET,TCP/FTP,TCP/SMTP,TCP/TIME :

Changed:  network address

--- #2

Was:
HOST : 192.5.21.2 : BRL-VLD : PDP-11/70 : UNIX : TCP/TELNET,TCP/SMTP,TCP/FTP,TCP/TIME :

Should be changed to:
HOST : 192.5.21.2 : BRL-VLD,VLD70 : PDP-11/70 : UNIX : TCP/TELNET,TCP/SMTP,TCP/FTP,TCP/TIME :

Changed:  added nicname "vld70".

--- #3

Was:
HOST : 192.5.21.6 : BRL-VGR : VAX-11/780 : UNIX : TCP/TELNET,TCP/SMTP,TCP/FTP,TCP/TIME :

Should be changed to:
HOST : 192.5.21.6 : BRL-VGR,VGR : VAX-11/780 : UNIX : TCP/TELNET,TCP/SMTP,TCP/FTP,TCP/TIME :

Changed:  added nicname "vgr"

---

Thanks very much!  The address change for the BRL-BMD machine is certainly
the most important and traumatic change of the bunch.  Now we really get
to see which machines can talk to class "C" networks!
			Cheers,
			 -Mike

Date: 17 November 1982 19:30-EST
From: Christopher C. Stacy <CSTACY at MIT-MC>
To: INFO-HOSTS at MIT-MC

Latest HOSTS table has new names for MINITS Chaosnet HUBs (formerly "Chaosnet TIPs").


   D          ;		    MIT/Stanford Host Table	-*-Mode: TEXT; NoFill: T-*-

; Last updated: MRC 3/15/83

;  The file <NETINFO>HOSTS.TXT at SRI-NIC is the official
; NIC Internet host table.  At one time it was totally inadequate
; for use at MIT and Stanford, hence this file, which is manually
; updated as necessary.  Eventually it will be replaced by HOSTS3
; and/or HOSTS4.

; The "official" versions are maintained as:
;	SYSTEM:HOSTS.TXT at SU-SCORE
;	SYSENG;HOSTS > at MIT-MC
;	HOSTS.TXT[HST,NET] at SU-AI

;  Modifications should be made to one of the official versions
; and a note of the change sent to INFO-HOSTS@SCORE.  If you
; cannot update all of the official versions it is crucial that
; INFO-HOSTS@SCORE be notified, otherwise your changes will be
; lost.

;  If you change the format or add a supported networks, PLEASE
; SEND MAIL to INFO-HOSTS@SCORE so the other systems which make
; use of this file have a chance to support your changes.

;  The easy way to compile the binary file and install it on
; the ITS systems is to run the batch command files:

; :XFILE SYSENG;HOSTS XFILE at MC

;  If you want to do it the hard way, read this file.  The
; other versions are installed manually from MC's.

; The network table is in the format of one line entries looking like:

; NET <name>,<network #>

; sorted alphabetically by network name.  All fields should be
; in upper case.  The fields are:

; <name>	official name of this network, as assigned by Jon
;		 Postel.

; <network #>	A single network number, in DECIMAL.  These
;		 numbers are assigned by Jon Postel.

; The host table is in the format of one line entries looking like:

; HOST <name>,<host #s>,<status>,<system>,<machine>,[<nicknames>]

; sorted alphabetically by host name.  All fields should be
; in upper case.  The fields are:

; <name>	official name of this site according to the
;		 NIC.

; <host #s>	A single <host #> or a list of them in
;		 brackets and separated by commas, with no
;		 spaces in between.
;
;		A <host #> is an OCTAL number, optionally
;		 preceded by a network name (ARPA, CHAOS, LCS,
;		 RCC, SU) and a space.  The default network
;		 name is ARPA.
;
; 		ARPANET host numbers are represented in as H/I
;		 where H and I are 8 bit DECIMAL numbers.  H is
;		 the host number, I is the IMP number.
;
;		Chaosnet host numbers are in octal.
;
;		LCSnet addresses are represented as LCS S/H,
;		 where S and H are 8 bit OCTAL numbers.  S is
;		 the LCSnet subnet, H is the host.
;
;		RCCnet addresses are in the same format as
;		 ARPANET addresses.
;
;		SUnet addresses are represented as SU S#H, where
;		 S and H are 8 bit OCTAL numbers.  S is the SUnet
;		 subnet, H is the host.

; <status>	whether USER or SERVER.  This is usually the
;		 status "according to the NIC".

; <system>	operating system name (e.g., TENEX, ITS,
;		 MULTICS, etc).  Hyphens do appear in the name,
;		 e.g. "TOPS-10" not "TOPS10".

; <machine>	actual machine type (e.g., PDP10, IBM-370, PDP11,
;		 etc).  By convention, KA-10, KI-10, KL-10,
;		 KL-20, Foonly and MAXC are all considered to be
;		 PDP-10s.  No - should be after "PDP"; this
;		 is so it fits in one 36-bit word.

; <nicknames>	nicknames for this host (whether NIC
;		 nicknames or local ones).  The list is in
;		 square brackets and each name is delimited
;		 by a comma.

; MIT subnet numbers...

; These do not appear in the binary host table, since no program
; needs to know them by name.  They are in this file since it
; seems like the most logical place to remember them.

; The following OCTAL numbers are MIT subnets.
;
;	0	Not to be used
;	1	Main campus Chaosnet
;	2	Tech Square Ethernet
;	3	MC IO 11 pseudo subnet (only MC PDP-10 is on this)
;	4	AI CHAOS 11 pseudo subnet (only AI PDP-10 is on this)
;	5	XX NETWORK 11 pseudo (DTE) subnet (only XX -20 is on this)
;	6	Tech Square Chaosnet
;	7	PFC link
;	10	Tech Square LCSnet
;	11	Tech Square asynchronous line net
;	12	Tech Square VII LCSnet
;	13	EE NETWORK 11 pseudo (DTE) subnet (only EECS -20 is on this)
;	14	Main campus Chaosnet (IN logical subnet)
;	15	Tech Square Chaosnet (IN logical subnet)
;	16	PFC Chaosnet (IN logical subnet)
;	17	West Campus Chaos subnet (Math Dept, ...)
;	20	CHAOS MIT IN subnet (ask JNC)
;	21	MIT Infinite Corridor Loop (JCF)
;	22	MIT Student Center Subnet
;	23	OZ CHAOS 11 pseudo subnet (only OZ -20 is on this)
;	24	SPEECH CHAOS 11 pseudo subnet (only SPEECH -20 on this)
;	25	EECS (38-3xx) Ethernet
;	26	Tech^2 Ninth floor/LCS Ethernet
;	27	Experimental asynchronous line net
;	30	Experimental radio broadcast net
;	31	Architecture Machine Group Chaos Ethernet
;	32	LCS Experimental EtherNet
;	33	SPEECH Ethernet (36-5xx)
;	34	EECS Chaos subnet (bldgs 36, 38, 39, 20)
;	35	East Campus Chaos subnet
;	36	SCRC Chaos subnet
;	37	SCRC-11 pseudo subnet (DR11)
;	40	SCRC-AI microwave link
;	41	Symbolics: Cambridge-Palo Alto  land line (SCRC<-->SPA)
;	42	Symbolics: Palo Alto-Chatsworth land line (SPA<-->SCH)
;	43	Symbolics: Palo Alto  local CHAOS    subnet (SPA)
;	44	Symbolics: Palo Alto  local Ethernet subnet (SPA)
;	45	Symbolics: Chatsworth local CHAOS    subnet (SCH)
;	46	Symbolics: Chatsworth local Ethernet subnet (SCH)
;	47	not used currently
;	50	Architecture Machine Group Ringnet Subnet
;	51	Symbolics Chaos Protocol Ethernet
;	52	Symbolics: Chatsworth  test CHAOS    subnet (SCH)
;	53	Symbolics: Chatsworth  test Ethernet subnet (SCH)

;  3 January 1984
;
; Changes, corrections, comments or questions to (COMP-FAC@SCRC-TENEX)
;
; The format of this file is documented in RFC 810, "DoD Internet
; Host Table Specification", which is available on-line at SRI-NIC
; as the file
;              [SRI-NIC]<NETINFO>RFC810.TXT
; It may be retrieved via FTP using username ANONYMOUS with
; any password.
;
; NOTE CAREFULLY: RFC 810 has been slightly revised since the original
; version was written.  In particular, the version printed in the
; "Internet Protocol Transition Notebook" does not document the
; added "machine type" field (between the host-name and system-name
; fields).
;
; The format for entries is:
;
; NET : NET-ADDR : NETNAME :
; GATEWAY : ADDR, ADDR : NAME : CPUTYPE : OPSYS : PROTOCOLS :
; HOST : ADDR, ALTERNATE-ADDR (if any): HOSTNAME,NICKNAME : CPUTYPE :
;   OPSYS : PROTOCOLS :
;
; Where:
;;  ADDR = internet address in decimal, e.g., 10.0.0.73
;;  CPUTYPE = machine type (PDP-11/70, VAX-11/780, FOONLY-F3, C/30, etc.)
;;  OPSYS = operating system (UNIX, TOPS-20, TENEX, ITS, etc.)
;;  PROTOCOLS = transport/service (NCP/FTP,TCP/TELNET,TCP/FTP, etc.)
;;  : (colon) = field delimiter
;;  :: (2 colons) = null field

;NET : 192.10.41.0 : SCRC-ETHERNET :

;  and Lisp Machines, you should make parallel changes to HOSTS >.  
;  When a change is made to HSTMIT (and HOSTS) a note of the change should
;  be sent to INFO-HOSTS@MC, preferably saying what you did.
;   
;  When some file changes and you want to compile the binary and
;  install on the ITS systems, run the batch command file
;   	:XFILE SYSENG;HOSTS XFILE  on MC.
;  This will assemble a HOSTS2 (old format) and HOSTS3 (new format)
;  binary, attempt to install the files on ML and DM, and send mail
;  to other host table maintainers at other systems.

; Last updated:	Hornig	26 April 1985

;  For compatibility with previous, still existing software on TOPS-20, Unix
;  and Lisp Machines, you should make parallel changes to HOSTS >.  
;  When a change is made to HSTMIT (and HOSTS) a note of the change should
;  be sent to INFO-HOSTS@MC, preferably saying what you did.
;   
;  When some file changes and you want to compile the binary and
;  install on the ITS systems, run the batch command file
;   	:XFILE SYSENG;HOSTS XFILE  on MC.
;  This will assemble a HOSTS2 (old format) and HOSTS3 (new format)
;  binary, attempt to install the files on ML and DM, and send mail
;  to other host table maintainers at other systems.
;
;
